<div id="review_18620949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18620949" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18620949?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781101058176" href="/book/show/9868468-a-song-for-arbonne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=canadian-lit">canadian-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18620949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14649272507028035093">A man I once loved introduced me to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/60177.Guy_Gavriel_Kay' title='Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Guy Gavriel Kay</a> just over twenty years ago. He started me off with his favourite, <i>A Song for Arbonne</i>, and it was enough to drag me into Kay's writing forever.<br/><br/>Over the years, I have returned again and again to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104101.The_Lions_of_Al_Rassan' title='The Lions of Al-Rassan by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lions of Al-Rassan</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana' title='Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tigana</a>, rereading these two favourites multiple times, but I have never really felt drawn back to the pages of J---'s favourite. A month ago, though, he came up in conversation right when I needed a new book to listen to, and wh</span>
  <span id="freeText14649272507028035093" style="display:none">A man I once loved introduced me to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/60177.Guy_Gavriel_Kay" title="Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Guy Gavriel Kay</a> just over twenty years ago. He started me off with his favourite, <i>A Song for Arbonne</i>, and it was enough to drag me into Kay's writing forever.<br /><br />Over the years, I have returned again and again to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104101.The_Lions_of_Al_Rassan" title="The Lions of Al-Rassan by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lions of Al-Rassan</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana" title="Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Tigana</a>, rereading these two favourites multiple times, but I have never really felt drawn back to the pages of J---'s favourite. A month ago, though, he came up in conversation right when I needed a new book to listen to, and when <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> popped up in my algorithm driven Audible suggestions, I didn't try to resist. I dove into this listen in the hope of finding what it was that J--- had loved so much all those years ago. <br /><br />Sadly, I don't think I figured out what J--- loved about <i>A Song for Arbonne</i>, but I think I have a better grip on the story for myself. <br /><br />It remains, for me, a very good but somewhat slight Guy Gavriel Kay book. It falls short of the emotional connections that touch me so deeply in <i>The Lions of Al-Rassan</i> (although I imagine it was quite the opposite for J---) and the ethical depths of <i>Tigana</i>. The former is driven by characters who came to life for me and remain alive no matter how often I read their story; the latter is masterwork that overturns the usual black and white simplicity of "fantasy" and delivers the single most convincing antagonist (some may call him "villain") of the genre.<br /><br /><i>A Song for Arbonne</i> doesn't hit either of those heights. Granted, the emotional superiority of <i>The Lions of Al-Rassan</i> (surely bolstered for me by the presence of the bisexual Ammar ibn Khairan) is entirely subjective, but the ethical superiority of <i>Tigana</i> is objectively the finest achievement of Kay's career, and I am comfortable placing both of my favourites at the top of any list of Guy Gavriel Kay's achievements. <br /><br /><i>A Song for Arbonne</i>, by contrast, is a little like a Fantasy Soap Opera, albeit a classy and well plotted one. Everyone knows everyone, or comes to know everyone, or links with all the important people, and everything tightens up into a neat little bow. This isn't to say that <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> is anything approaching poor. It is really an excellent book, and there are characters and moments all over <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> that deserve a reader's love -- from the brooding Blaise de Garsenc and the emotionally scarred Bertran de Talaire to the power and strength of Arbonne's women and the surprisingly exciting canoeing game on the wild river at night. Moreover, <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> includes some quite glorious Fantasy poetry from Guy Gavriel Kay, injected into the tale as the songs of the troubadors (and Euan Morton's unaccompanied singing of these songs in the audio version is the highlight of his wonderful narration). But even with all of these top notch elements, <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> can't help but fall short of Kay's best works for me.<br /><br />I am glad I came back to the place where my love for Guy Gavriel Kay began, and even more pleased that if put me in mind of J--- again after so long. I feel like <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> will push me to read the couple of Kay books I have been ignoring, in much the same way it once sent me on a voracious consuming of everything he had published twenty years ago. It is, regardless of my inability to love it, the sort of book that inspires me to read on. But will I move on to his books inspired by Ancient China or simply return to my beloved <i>Lions of Al-Rassan</i>? I hope the former but probably the latter. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14649272507028035093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1230234535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230234535" />
    <a title="Nicholas Kotar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5853754-nicholas-kotar"><img alt="Nicholas Kotar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422802815p2/5853754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230234535?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicholas Kotar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicholas Kotar" href="/user/show/5853754-nicholas-kotar">Nicholas Kotar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230234535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6989427114110326729">How I found this book is a story in itself. A few years ago I was living in what basically amounted to a "boarding university" (not merely a dorm, but all the restrictions you'd expect at a closed campus boarding school somewhere in North England) The guy living next door, who impressed me before only with the incredible number of days he could go without showering, unexpectedly impressed me with his reading materials. In a burst of gratitude that I helped him figure out how to play something on</span>
  <span id="freeText6989427114110326729" style="display:none">How I found this book is a story in itself. A few years ago I was living in what basically amounted to a "boarding university" (not merely a dorm, but all the restrictions you'd expect at a closed campus boarding school somewhere in North England) The guy living next door, who impressed me before only with the incredible number of days he could go without showering, unexpectedly impressed me with his reading materials. In a burst of gratitude that I helped him figure out how to play something on an old plug-in organ he found goodness knows where, He offered me any book I liked in his room. I had not read Kay before, but the cover intrigued me.<br /><br />Inconveniently (it was finals time) I couldn't put the book down. Great main character, a really loathsome bad guy (almost too loathsome for my tastes), and an obvious love for the Middle Ages that I found extremely refreshing. Especially with George R. R. Martin's love/hate relationship with the Middle Ages, reading a book that considers the brutality of the age honestly, but manages still to revel in a distinctly medieval aesthetic, was wonderful. <br /><br />The female characters, however, were probably the best part of this book. Kay tackles issues modern issues sexism with nuance and humanity. But best of all is his ability to develop truly strong women characters without resorting to "female breastplates" (those who read the hilarious i09.com article on this will know what I mean), which are all too common today. I have no problem with women warriors, I just like a bit of verisimilitude, even in fantasies. <br /><br />And of course, as a singer, any story set in a land of minstrels is just fine by me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6989427114110326729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1045068622" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1045068622" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3269646-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469570174p2/3269646.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1045068622?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/3269646-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1045068622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5905566429651334603">This is a generous five stars, to be honest. It is based on the prose and the characters and the worldbuilding. The plot itself isn't much, and should bring the book to four stars, but I can't bring myself to do so, because the writing was so beautifully crafted. I love GGK's rhythm and word choice, and his ability to evoke a feeling with just a sentence. Stunning.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1045068622">
  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer10619266881944416414">My 4th Kay book this year, I just cannot stop reading him.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104085.A_Song_for_Arbonne' title='A Song for Arbonne by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Song for Arbonne</a> is set in a Provencal atmosphere, so similar to 12th century France you can smell the fields of flowers and hear the soft playing of music as you read. So beautiful, yet brutal, as those times were known. There lies the problem of not being able to give this one 5 stars. The world was so built out, and as I said beautiful, there was no room for me to love, really love or truly hate (except that nasty Galbert de Garsenc)</span>
  <span id="freeText10619266881944416414" style="display:none">My 4th Kay book this year, I just cannot stop reading him.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104085.A_Song_for_Arbonne" title="A Song for Arbonne by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">A Song for Arbonne</a> is set in a Provencal atmosphere, so similar to 12th century France you can smell the fields of flowers and hear the soft playing of music as you read. So beautiful, yet brutal, as those times were known. There lies the problem of not being able to give this one 5 stars. The world was so built out, and as I said beautiful, there was no room for me to love, really love or truly hate (except that nasty Galbert de Garsenc) any of the characters. *sigh*. I wanted to embrace Bertran de Talair, the kind of man I always fell for in my youth. I wanted to take Blaise by the hand and lead him to his destiny. I just got too lost in the beauty of the land to bother with anything else.<br /><br />Onward I go. I know I said I would read all of his books in publication order, however, It was not even 2 years ago that I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104101.The_Lions_of_Al_Rassan" title="The Lions of Al-Rassan by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lions of Al-Rassan</a>, and so I am by-passing it and moving on to the next in line -<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104097.Sailing_to_Sarantium__The_Sarantine_Mosaic___1_" title="Sailing to Sarantium (The Sarantine Mosaic, #1) by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Sailing to Sarantium</a>.</span>

<div id="review_821400524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/821400524" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7177008-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388366904p2/7177008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/821400524?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/7177008-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780517593127" href="/book/show/533820.A_Song_For_Arbonne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=middle-ages">middle-ages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821400524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14490686386769574634">An enchanting, highly recommended historical fantasy that pulled me into the world of Provence, land of 'courts of love' and of troubadours, and other kingdoms or dukedoms of medieval France, with Kay using each civilization as a basis for his fantasy concept of these places. The story begins and ends with excerpts from the written 'vidans' or lives of two of Arbonne's most famous troubadours: "the first and perhaps most famous", Anselme of Cauvas and ending with that of Lisseut of Vezét, the la</span>
  <span id="freeText14490686386769574634" style="display:none">An enchanting, highly recommended historical fantasy that pulled me into the world of Provence, land of 'courts of love' and of troubadours, and other kingdoms or dukedoms of medieval France, with Kay using each civilization as a basis for his fantasy concept of these places. The story begins and ends with excerpts from the written 'vidans' or lives of two of Arbonne's most famous troubadours: "the first and perhaps most famous", Anselme of Cauvas and ending with that of Lisseut of Vezét, the latter a main character in the novel. She apparently becomes a famous woman troubadour. As prologue, twenty-three years before the action starts, there are a love triangle involving a husband, Duke Urté, his wife, Aelis, and her lover, Duke Bertran, a birth, and Aelis's death in childbirth. The two dukes have maintained their hatred of each other all these years, which has poisoned the atmosphere in Arbonne and led to internal strife. The novel takes place over the course of a year, with each of the four sections named after a season. In spring, into this country of music and courtly love, rides the protagonist, the mercenary soldier Blaise of Gorhaut, fleeing his native land. Gorhaut is a rival kingdom to the north, a cruel, implacable place, as opposed to the softer Arbonne. Blaise hates what his kingdom has become after the unfair agreement with another kingdom; that treaty and its influence on the action is mentioned again and again. A most unpleasant person, the present king, Ademar, has usurped the throne. War between the two countries is inevitable, the final battle fought on the shores of a lake; Arbonne fights for its very life. Interwoven is the story of Lisseut. <br /><br />There's everything you could wish for in a novel: secrets, bravery, cowardice, treachery, deceit, love, hope. I liked learning something of the Provençal culture. The story took awhile to 'take off', but by the 'Autumn' section, it really picked up after intermittent slow spots. Some of the psychology was implausible, especially that of the archvillain. Blaise was a good man and heroic, but how EVERY woman [or so it seemed] could be attracted to him, I don't understand. He was well-fleshed out, but many of the others were only no more than tokens: the stalwart companions; the absolute villains, with no redeeming qualities; the nobility; the priests and priestesses. I enjoyed the two one-on-one duels to the death. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14490686386769574634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2140920600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140920600" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2140920600?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780517593127" href="/book/show/533820.A_Song_For_Arbonne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140920600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3943973928740968290"><i>”Until the sun dies and the moons fall, Gorhaut and Arbonne shall not lie easily beside each other.”</i><br/><br/>This is my third book by Guy Gavriel Kay and, while all have been excellent, this one is my favorite so far. I give that qualifier because there are more Kay books to read and with every story he manages to enthrall me all over again. In each book he has managed to make his fictionalized lands seem real and familiar by evoking the memories of our world’s own past. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana' title='Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tigana</a> conjures visions of mediev</span>
  <span id="freeText3943973928740968290" style="display:none"><i>”Until the sun dies and the moons fall, Gorhaut and Arbonne shall not lie easily beside each other.”</i><br /><br />This is my third book by Guy Gavriel Kay and, while all have been excellent, this one is my favorite so far. I give that qualifier because there are more Kay books to read and with every story he manages to enthrall me all over again. In each book he has managed to make his fictionalized lands seem real and familiar by evoking the memories of our world’s own past. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana" title="Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Tigana</a> conjures visions of medieval Italy and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104097.Sailing_to_Sarantium__The_Sarantine_Mosaic___1_" title="Sailing to Sarantium (The Sarantine Mosaic, #1) by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Sailing to Sarantium</a> calls ancient Constantinople to mind. This time, Kay presents the beautiful land of Arbonne which closely resembles medieval Provence. Bordered on the north by Gorhaut, Arbonne soon finds itself threatened by both political machinations in that country as well as by long-running schisms within its own borders.<br /><br />Kay weaves a masterful story, told with elegant and moving prose, that touches upon the hurts and betrayals inflicted upon the largest of political stages as well as the potentially more damaging ones borne on far more personal fronts. There is a sizable cast of characters but readers can’t help but be drawn into their lives and moved, for good or ill, by their actions. I was riveted from the beginning and had to make myself put the book down sometimes to attend to real life. <br /><br />There is almost a bittersweet quality to Kay’s storytelling. I don’t think he strives to give readers endings that are 100% purely happy. And it might be that emotional closure isn’t always on offer either. But that’s real life, isn’t it? I always say that I rarely hand out five stars to books. A story has to create an emotional reaction in me, something deep and true, in order to squeeze that fifth star from me. This story - full of song and violence, love and hate, old betrayals and new alliances, desecrations and redemptions - managed to move me to tears when I was not expecting it. So, true to my word, five stars it is. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3943973928740968290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1906594293" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1906594293" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2445786-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245681908p2/2445786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1906594293?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/2445786-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2445786-olivia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1906594293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14339730166767703469">Guy Gavriel Kay has the kind of prose that makes me want to bury myself and cry because I'll never be able to write like him. A Song for Arbonne has everything: romance, troubadours, intrigue, war, passion, revenge. It's an epic story. <br/><br/>Guy Gavriel Kay writes something I wouldn't call fantasy but more alternative history. He takes a place (here it's the lovely Provence) then does his research and sets a story in an alternative version of it. Beautiful plot, great characters and a lot of heartbrea</span>
  <span id="freeText14339730166767703469" style="display:none">Guy Gavriel Kay has the kind of prose that makes me want to bury myself and cry because I'll never be able to write like him. A Song for Arbonne has everything: romance, troubadours, intrigue, war, passion, revenge. It's an epic story. <br /><br />Guy Gavriel Kay writes something I wouldn't call fantasy but more alternative history. He takes a place (here it's the lovely Provence) then does his research and sets a story in an alternative version of it. Beautiful plot, great characters and a lot of heartbreak.<br /><br />There were a few things I liked less about this book. The antagonists seem to be evil, just to be evil and I couldn't really find a motive. I find a villain who is a villain just so there's a villain a bit unsatisfying. And I wasn't happy with the resolution at the end, but maybe that was just me.<br /><br />Definitely a must read for all GGK fans. If you haven't read any of his work yet, I suggest you start with The Lions of Al-Rassan. It made me sob into my pillow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14339730166767703469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229593651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229593651" />
    <a title="Shy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3094614-shy"><img alt="Shy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419064291p2/3094614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229593651?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shy" href="/user/show/3094614-shy">Shy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11466357-a-song-for-arbonne">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=on-kindle">on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3094614-shy?shelf=genre_speculative-fantasy">genre_speculative-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229593651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7288558369640614743">This was my first exposure to Kay's work, and I've to say that I've already fallen in love with his writing. <br/><br/>In <i>A Song for Arbonne</i>, he created a dazzling and extraordinary tale of mere mortals, whose life were entangled by malevolence, political intrigue and love. From this overtly distinct mix, Kay managed to weave such a convoluted story that acquire a life of its own. This, coupled with the story's multi-layered characters, interesting plot and Kay's very own magnificent prose produced an awe</span>
  <span id="freeText7288558369640614743" style="display:none">This was my first exposure to Kay's work, and I've to say that I've already fallen in love with his writing. <br /><br />In <i>A Song for Arbonne</i>, he created a dazzling and extraordinary tale of mere mortals, whose life were entangled by malevolence, political intrigue and love. From this overtly distinct mix, Kay managed to weave such a convoluted story that acquire a life of its own. This, coupled with the story's multi-layered characters, interesting plot and Kay's very own magnificent prose produced an awe-inspiring, emotional and immensely satisfying novel. <br /><br />If you are among those who enjoy historical fiction, sprinkled with a little bit of magical element, I dare say that reading Kay's <i>A Song for Arbonne</i> is a definite must. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7288558369640614743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_117094576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117094576" />
    <a title="Blake Charlton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2698100-blake-charlton"><img alt="Blake Charlton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442492307p2/2698100.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117094576?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blake Charlton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blake Charlton" href="/user/show/2698100-blake-charlton">Blake Charlton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117094576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10687086733888409734">i have been avoiding ASfA for a while now, mostly because i couldn't conceive of how he might turn a novel based on the courtly love into anything other then...well...courtly mush. i'm happy to report that GGK with his typical brilliants takes the subject, scrutinizes it, and transformed it into a wonderful narrative. i did have a few objections: the plurality of characters sometimes ran out of control and i had to double back to get the names straight, distractingly so; and the "evil male-domin</span>
  <span id="freeText10687086733888409734" style="display:none">i have been avoiding ASfA for a while now, mostly because i couldn't conceive of how he might turn a novel based on the courtly love into anything other then...well...courtly mush. i'm happy to report that GGK with his typical brilliants takes the subject, scrutinizes it, and transformed it into a wonderful narrative. i did have a few objections: the plurality of characters sometimes ran out of control and i had to double back to get the names straight, distractingly so; and the "evil male-dominated kingdom is evil" was a bit heavy handed at times. but otherwise, GGK delivered a wonderful narrative with rich history that in any lesser artists hands would have become drab.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10687086733888409734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CPdGL2yde6oViGwA/xjX9TCcIIpwK6/ShPcVOhiQcKl6bqG2fDmYysIT9Ye+2YmiRYzoY9uQgGFGSOIv54X8Pg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ovlNZ46D4L5l6wCxxtRnMpd/uWF/1pF6zT6TLrb6G73QYKr+nicD3rJwmTaHFTll4m9xiNRtvskPgWQ7Se+XKg==')})
  }

Elric of Melniboné follows Yrkoon\'s scheming, reaching its climax in a battle between Elric and Yrkoon with the demonic runeblades Stormbringer and Mournblade. The writing of its members is in marked contrast to their robust active personalities. The poems Andrić published before WWI are virtually indistinguishable in tone from much of what his contemporaries were writing. Nevertheless, it\'s probably true to say that in his case the role of the political activist, however sincerely he played it at the time, was fundamentally unsuited to him. By contrast, however, the prevailing melancholy seemed to match his temperamental reponse to the world.\n These early poems point in no particular direction, beyond establishing the free verse form of virtually all of Andrić’s poetry and a tendency to a mournful self-pity which sometimes threatens his personal statements.\n The prose poems written during the War represent a personal conffesion &amp; cannot be considered merely the reflection of a literary vogue. “Ex Ponto” (refers to Ovid’s account of his Black Sea exile) was published in 1918; “Unrest” in 1920, when “Ex Ponto” was already reprinted. Thereafter Andrić refused to allow them to be included in any of his collections of his works published before his death. He rejected them because they seemed to him too intimate. But, they\'re important since they contain ideas &amp; themes which recur in his later works.\n The strong emotional colouring was toned down in Andrić’s later prose poems &amp; verse but their form, a combination of aphoristic statements &amp; longer reflective passages, continued to appeal to him. “Ex Ponto” &amp; “Unrest” record his emotional reaction to the circumstances of his early life &amp; the development of a number of themes around the central paradox of his personality &amp; work.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11034765874654676745\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17330285704282109248">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categoriz</span>
  <span id="freeText17330285704282109248" style="display:none">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categorization when possible.</span>
